CVE-2021-3129
(9.8 CRITICAL)

EPSS: 97.48%

2 posts

Ignition before 2.5.2, as used in Laravel and other products, allows unauthenticated remote attackers to execute arbitrary code because of insecure usage of file_get_contents() and file_put_contents(). This is exploitable on sites using debug mode with Laravel before 8.4.2.

CVE-2023-46604
(9.8 CRITICAL)

EPSS: 97.15%

4 posts

The Java OpenWire protocol marshaller is vulnerable to Remote Code Execution. This vulnerability may allow a remote attacker with network access to either a Java-based OpenWire broker or client to run arbitrary shell commands by manipulating serialized class types in the OpenWire protocol to cause either the client or the broker (respectively) to instantiate any class on the classpath. CVE-2023-27524
(9.8 CRITICAL)

EPSS: 96.23%

5 posts

Session Validation attacks in Apache Superset versions up to and including 2.0.1. Installations that have not altered the default configured SECRET_KEY according to installation instructions allow for an attacker to authenticate and access unauthorized resources. This does not affect Superset administrators who have changed the default value for SECRET_KEY config.

simontsui at 2023-12-29T19:05:48.240Z [@kpwn](https://infosec.exchange/@kpwn) CVE-2023-20198 was fascinating for many reasons: * Cisco is a networking vendor giant. Almost every organization had an affected device. * CVSSv3 score of 10.0 is rare for an established product, especially from Cisco. 10.0 is the equivalent of leaving the backdoor wide open, but no one else saw the possibility? * There was no patch available at the time of disclosure. First available patch was 6 days later, and for one specific model. * The identified implant was detected on approximately 40,000-60,000 compromised devices. * An operation of this scale screams nation state activity, but no one was pointing fingers (or taking credit). * The likely use of that many devices is for a botnet. However, nothing was done with the infected hosts. Either the threat actor was a solo operation or wanted to lay low after attracting international attention. * Cisco PSIRT couldn't figure out how the threat actor uploaded the implant. This was eventually identified as the other zero-day CVE-2023-20273. * There was a industrial control system angle to this, when Rockwell Automation announced that they were impacted by CVE-2023-20198 (admitting to CVE-2023-20273 later too) [#CveCrowdDeny](https://infosec.exchange/tags/CveCrowdDeny)

harrysintonen at 2024-01-01T16:15:30.976Z Media keeps parroting the grossly misleading information about [#Terrapin](https://infosec.exchange/tags/Terrapin) attack (CVE-2023-48795). This vulnerability is only a significant problem with versions of AsyncSSH that have other serious flaws that actually allow meaningful exploitation. For the rest the only issue is downgrading the SSH Extension Negotiation. While this is theory will allow removing the restrictions set on the used signature algorithms, you'd still also need to have a client and server that both agree to use an algorithm that has a grave security flaw in it. This is not very likely. Removal of the keystroke timing countermeasures has very little practical impact as you'd still need to actually perform the timing attack to exploit this (and this extension was added for OpenSSH 9.5 to begin with, earlier versions don't even attempt to use this extension so there is nothing to attack against there). I don't know why it is so difficult for media to get this right. Crying wolf for non-issues keeps diluting the messaging about actually impactful security issues. Of course the security updates should be installed in a timely manner, especially if AsyncSSH is being used. But the messaging around Terrapin has been overly alarmistic, and not very helpful as a whole. [https://thehackernews.com/2024/01/new-terrapin-flaw-could-let- attackers.html](https://thehackernews.com/2024/01/new-terrapin-flaw-could-let- attackers.html)

simontsui at 2023-12-29T19:05:48.240Z [@kpwn](https://infosec.exchange/@kpwn) CVE-2023-20198 was fascinating for many reasons: * Cisco is a networking vendor giant. Almost every organization had an affected device. * CVSSv3 score of 10.0 is rare for an established product, especially from Cisco. 10.0 is the equivalent of leaving the backdoor wide open, but no one else saw the possibility? * There was no patch available at the time of disclosure. First available patch was 6 days later, and for one specific model. * The identified implant was detected on approximately 40,000-60,000 compromised devices. * An operation of this scale screams nation state activity, but no one was pointing fingers (or taking credit). * The likely use of that many devices is for a botnet. However, nothing was done with the infected hosts. Either the threat actor was a solo operation or wanted to lay low after attracting international attention. * Cisco PSIRT couldn't figure out how the threat actor uploaded the implant. This was eventually identified as the other zero-day CVE-2023-20273. * There was a industrial control system angle to this, when Rockwell Automation announced that they were impacted by CVE-2023-20198 (admitting to CVE-2023-20273 later too) [#CveCrowdDeny](https://infosec.exchange/tags/CveCrowdDeny)

CVE-2022-1471
(9.8 CRITICAL)

EPSS: 0.58%

6 posts

SnakeYaml's Constructor() class does not restrict types which can be instantiated during deserialization.¬†Deserializing yaml content provided by an attacker can lead to remote code execution. We recommend using SnakeYaml's SafeConsturctor when parsing untrusted content to restrict deserialization. We recommend upgrading to version 2.0 and beyond.

CVE-2023-7102
(9.8 CRITICAL)

EPSS: 0.10%

2 posts

Use of a Third Party library produced a vulnerability in Barracuda Networks Inc. Barracuda ESG Appliance which allowed Parameter Injection.This issue affected Barracuda ESG Appliance, from 5.1.3.001 through 9.2.1.001, until Barracuda removed the vulnerable logic.

simontsui at 2023-12-28T21:04:33.081Z [@nuddlegg](https://fosstodon.org/@nuddlegg) Le Dinh Hai provided the proof of concept for CVE-2023-7101 back in March 2023: [https://github.com/haile01/perl_spreadsheet_excel_rce_poc/tree/main](https://github.com/haile01/perl_spreadsheet_excel_rce_poc/tree/main) As [@0x009AD6_810](https://infosec.exchange/@0x009AD6_810) noted in a [tweet](https://twitter.com/0x009AD6_810/status/1740034318205178024), "CVE-2023-7101 was discovered in ESG and probably weaponized as an exploit + payload." Barracuda noted that this vulnerability was exploited against their ESG Appliance: [https://www.barracuda.com/company/legal/esg- vulnerability](https://www.barracuda.com/company/legal/esg-vulnerability) A question arises: Should CVE-2023-7101 also be added to CISA's Known Exploited Vulnerabilities Catalog when CVE-2023-7102 (the identical vulnerability introduced to a Barracuda product) was confirmed to be exploited? CISA won't add an exploited vulnerability to its Catalog if there isn't a clear remediation action for the vulnerability, such as a vendor-provided update.

CVE-2021-43566
(2.5 LOW)

EPSS: 0.09%

2 posts

All versions of Samba prior to 4.13.16 are vulnerable to a malicious client using an SMB1 or NFS race to allow a directory to be created in an area of the server file system not exported under the share definition. Note that SMB1 has to be enabled, or the share also available via NFS in order for this attack to succeed.

(7.8 HIGH)

This issue is fixed in watchOS 9.5.2, macOS Big Sur 11.7.8, iOS 15.7.7 and iPadOS 15.7.7, macOS Monterey 12.6.7, watchOS 8.8.1, iOS 16.5.1 and iPadOS 16.5.1, macOS Ventura 13.4.1. CVE-2023-38545
(9.8 CRITICAL)

EPSS: 0.07%

2 posts

This flaw makes curl overflow a heap based buffer in the SOCKS5 proxy handshake. When curl is asked to pass along the host name to the SOCKS5 proxy to allow that to resolve the address instead of it getting done by curl itself, the maximum length that host name can be is 255 bytes. If the host name is detected to be longer, curl switches to local name resolving and instead passes on the resolved

BitLocker Security Feature Bypass Vulnerability

fencepost at 2024-01-10T18:03:54.668Z I have to admit, my immediate thoughts on the Bitlocker/WinRE vulnerability (local access required) were: 1) Oh hey, recovery without TPM sniffing 2) Reasons why you need to be able to remote-clear the TPM on managed remote devices (e.g. remote user laptops). 3) Reasons why Bitlocker alone isn't enough for situations where security is required vs security theater. Threat models matter. CVE: [https://msrc.microsoft.com/update- guide/vulnerability/CVE-2024-20666](https://msrc.microsoft.com/update- guide/vulnerability/CVE-2024-20666) "BitLocker Security Feature Bypass Vulnerability"

CVE-2024-22165
(6.5 MEDIUM)

EPSS: 0.00%

2 posts

In Splunk Enterprise Security (ES) versions lower than 7.1.2, an attacker can create a malformed Investigation to perform a denial of service (DoS). The malformed investigation prevents the generation and rendering of the Investigations manager until it is deleted.
The vulnerability requires an authenticated session and access to create an Investigation. It only affects the availability of the

nbwpuk at 2024-01-09T15:46:05.049Z Important Security Notice: WordPress administrators being actively targeted with phishing campaign It has come to our attention that a fraudulent phishing campaign is actively targeting administrators of WordPress websites. The attackers are sending emails with the subject line "URGENT: Vulnerability found - Your website [DOMAIN] is at risk!" The email claims to be from the WordPress Security Team and insists on addressing a critical Remote Code Execution (RCE) vulnerability affecting your website. It urges users to download a plugin labelled as "CVE-2024-46188 Patch" to mitigate the alleged threat. READ MORE: [https://encode.host/announcements/64/Important-Security-Notice- WordPress-administrators-being-actively-targeted-with-phishing- campaign.html](https://encode.host/announcements/64/Important-Security-Notice- WordPress-administrators-being-actively-targeted-with-phishing-campaign.html) [#WordPress](https://infosec.exchange/tags/WordPress) [#security](https://infosec.exchange/tags/security) [#malware](https://infosec.exchange/tags/malware) [#phishing](https://infosec.exchange/tags/phishing)
jamez@jamez.it at 2024-01-05T18:23:34.000Z I‚Äôve received this email: [[üñº jamez.it/blog/wp-content/uploa‚Ä¶]](https://jamez.it/blog/wp- content/uploads/2024/01/image.png) If you follow the link to phishing URL https://us.en- wordpress.org/plugins/cve-2024-46188/, download the file, and analyze the code, you immediately realize that this plugin is malicious and does the following: * it creates an admin user, where the username is a function of the website URL on which the plugin is installed, and the password is deterministic (E5rLDmno9F), although obtained by shuffling a string; * it makes that user unsearchable from the WP interface; * it makes the plugin unsearchable from the WP interface; * it pings home (https://defcve.com/wpapi?siteurl=, again some shuffling happens to hide this) to let the scammers know when someone ‚Äúbites‚Äù; * it downloads [P.A.S. fork](https://github.com/cr1f/P.A.S.-Fork/tree/main) from home and saves it to disk. Pretending to be the Red Cross to perform a sneak attack is one of the vilest things a human being can do. Stay safe, kids, always be paranoid and never trust a famous logo. CVE-2024-21633
(7.8 HIGH)

EPSS: 0.00%

2 posts

Apktool is a tool for reverse engineering Android APK files. In versions 2.9.1 and prior, Apktool infers resource files' output path according to their resource names which can be manipulated by attacker to place files at desired location on the system Apktool runs on. Affected environments are those in which an attacker may write/overwrite any file that user has write access, and either user name
